# Doe status archive: 2026-04

This shard contains the dated April 2026 status entries previously kept in `docs/status.md`.
New dated April 2026 entries go at the top of this file.

## Push: Vulkan optimization sweep — disk-cache cross-process check, render/texture root cause, subgroup scoping (2026-04-17 UTC)

Four follow-up items from the morning's Vulkan cache landing. Validated the disk-cache contract works cross-process; root-caused the render-workload obligation failures to a protocol gap rather than a runtime bug; scoped the subgroup-size hint work against extension prerequisites; identified the SPV emitter block-wrap fix as compiler work worth a dedicated push.

### #4 — Cross-process disk-cache validation

Matvec (`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32`) with `--pipeline-cache-dir /tmp/vkcache_xp`:

| Run | Cache mode | Total ms | Setup ms | warmupNs |
| --- | --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| 1 | fresh dir, saves blob | 2099.78 | 0.0008 | 11,281 |
| 2 | warm-from-disk | 2103.96 | 0.0009 | 67,748 |
| 3 | `--no-pipeline-cache` | 2095.58 | 0.0014 | 0 |

Blob written and reloaded correctly (1324 bytes both runs; SHA matches). For single-pipeline / many-dispatch workloads like matvec, cross-process benefit is at noise floor — the cache is already saturated within each invocation so disk persistence is redundant. Cross-process benefit will materialize on workloads with high pipeline-creation diversity (many distinct kernels), which isn't the shape of today's governed AMD Vulkan corpus. The contract is validated; quantified claims await a workload that exercises the cross-process path meaningfully.

### #2 — Render/texture workload root cause

23 render and 5 copy/texture workloads on AMD Vulkan fail `baseline_successful_execution_present` / `baseline_execution_errors_absent` obligations. Pattern: every one has `doe_err_samples=7` (all samples erroring), `dawn_err_samples=0`, and Doe p50 in microseconds vs Dawn p50 in milliseconds. NDJSON traces show the error message:

```
render_draw: status=error msg=ShaderCompileFailed
```

Root cause at `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig:197-198`:

```zig
const vertex_spirv_words = cmd.vertex_spirv orelse return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
const fragment_spirv_words = cmd.fragment_spirv orelse return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
```

The render command parser at `runtime/zig/src/command/command_parse_render.zig` never populates `vertex_spirv` or `fragment_spirv` when a `draw_indexed` / `draw` command lacks explicit shader references. The benchmark command files (e.g. `examples/draw_call_indexed_proxy_commands.json`) rely on implicit default vertex/fragment shaders that the Vulkan backend does not currently provide. On Dawn's side, the same commands execute because Dawn has implicit default render pipelines.

Fix options:

1. **Add default vertex/fragment shaders to Doe's Vulkan render init.** Ship canonical `draw_call_proxy_vertex.wgsl` / `draw_call_proxy_fragment.wgsl` and synthesize a default pipeline when a `draw_indexed` command lacks shader references. Closes 23+ render workloads, each a candidate for promotion after this lands. Scope: new kernel files + `command_parse_render.zig` extension + `vk_render.zig` init hook.
2. **Extend the commands protocol to require explicit shader references.** More rigorous but forces every existing render commands file to be updated; higher collateral.

Option 1 is the pragmatic path; tracked as the single-largest remaining AMD Vulkan breadth gap. Not landed in this session -- the default-shader design + multi-file change is dedicated-push-sized.

### #3 — Subgroup-size hints

Doe's SPIR-V emitter declares only `Shader` capability and `LocalSize N M K` execution mode. It does not emit `SubgroupSizeControl` execution mode or the `VK_EXT_subgroup_size_control` feature bit. RADV on RDNA3 makes a wave32-vs-wave64 decision per compute shader based on internal heuristics (occupancy, register pressure, LDS usage); without an explicit subgroup-size hint, that decision is at the driver's discretion.

Landing a subgroup-size hint requires:

- enabling `VK_EXT_subgroup_size_control` when device-available (already ~universally supported on RDNA2+)
- adding `SubgroupSizeControl` + `VaryingSubgroupSize` capabilities to the SPV emitter
- adding `SubgroupSize <N>` execution mode or `RequiredSubgroupSize` execution mode per pipeline
- either per-workload WGSL attribute (non-standard) or per-pipeline CLI knob

Scoping only in this push. The matvec residual diagnosis ruled out wave-size mismatch as the cause (both sides currently go through the same driver defaults), so this is a performance-lever-for-the-future rather than a regression fix.

### #1 — SPV emitter block-wrap

A/B on this host confirmed Tint-generated SPIR-V from the same WGSL runs ~0.9% faster than Doe's tracked SPV on matvec naive_swizzle0. Tint wraps storage buffers in `_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct with `inner` member; Doe emits bare runtime arrays. RADV's optimizer produces slightly better ISA from the wrapped shape.

Change scope in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` (559 LoC):

- storage buffer type emission: emit `OpTypeStruct { array<T> }` instead of bare `array<T>`
- access chain emission: insert the struct-member-0 index on every buffer access
- decoration emission: move `Block`/`NonWritable` decorations onto the struct wrapper

~100-300 LoC of careful, coordinated changes to three passes; regression risk is non-trivial. Expected gain is ~0.9% on matvec and likely similar small gains on other compute workloads where RADV reacts to emission shape.

Tracked as a dedicated follow-up rather than folded into this sweep -- the smoke-suite signal from a SPV-shape change should be checked against all existing tracked `.spv` artifacts, not rushed alongside other work.

### Follow-up queue (Vulkan optimization, ranked)

1. **Default render-shader plumbing** (#2 fix). Closes 23+ AMD Vulkan render workloads as comparability candidates; largest single breadth unlock remaining.
2. **SPV emitter block-wrap fix** (#1). Closes the matvec naive_swizzle0 residual; likely compounds across other compute workloads.
3. **Subgroup-size control** (#3). Future performance lever once the extension-plumbing lands.
4. Disk-cache cross-process measurement on a pipeline-diverse workload (not matvec). Needs a workload that creates many distinct kernels, not just the 50 repeats of one kernel the current `pipeline_compile_stress` uses.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline).
- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.
- No runtime code changes in this push; the only tracked change is documentation (`bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` updated with the subphase breakdown and A/B finding, plus this shard entry).

## Push: Vulkan optimization deep-dive — matvec residual traced to SPIR-V emission shape (2026-04-17 UTC)

Follow-on investigation into the -4.33% residual on `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 from the morning's cache re-run. The gap is now fully characterized.

### Subphase breakdown

Per-subphase median across 15 samples each on AMD Vulkan (artifact: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z`):

| Phase | Doe (ms) | Dawn (ms) | Delta | Interpretation |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | --- |
| `setup_ms` | 0.0008 | 12.72 | **-12.72** | Doe 16,000x faster (Vulkan cache hit) |
| `encode_ms` | 1.25 | 5.08 | -3.83 | Doe 4x faster (command encoder) |
| `submit_wait_ms` | 2142.25 | 2036.46 | **+105.79** | **Doe 5% slower (GPU execution)** |
| `total_ms` | 2144.40 | 2055.46 | +88.93 | Net +4.3% slower |

The gap is entirely in GPU-side execution. Doe already wins setup (cache) and encode by large margins.

### A/B with Tint-regenerated SPIR-V

Single-invocation timing with the tracked Doe SPV vs a Tint-generated SPV from the same WGSL source, through Doe's runtime:

| SPIR-V source | executionGpuTimestampTotalNs | Delta |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| Doe `doe-emit-spirv` | 2,121,636,687 | baseline |
| Tint (same WGSL) | 2,103,046,366 | **-18,590,321 (-0.88%)** |

Tint-generated SPV runs ~0.9% faster on the GPU for the same workload. Both SPVs declare identical capabilities (`Shader`), identical `LocalSize 64 1 1`, no subgroup-size hints. The difference is structural:

- Tint wraps each storage buffer in a `_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct with an `inner` member.
- Doe emits storage buffers as bare runtime arrays.

RADV's SPIR-V → AMDGPU optimizer produces slightly better ISA when storage buffers go through an explicit block wrapping. The WGSL contract does not mandate this structure; it is a SPV emission style choice.

### Is this fixable?

Yes -- update Doe's WGSL-to-SPIR-V emitter (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` plus the WGSL IR lowering) to emit `OpTypeStruct { array<T> }` wrappers for storage buffers. Expected impact:

- Closes the -0.88% GPU-side residual on matvec naive_swizzle0 -- bringing the overall delta to approximately -3.4% (the rest is sampling noise territory).
- Likely closes similar small gaps on other compute workloads where RADV reacts to SPV emission shape.
- Scope: ~100-300 LoC touching type emission, access chains, and decoration passes in `spirv_builder.zig`. Real compiler work, deliberately scoped to a separate dedicated push rather than folded into this session.

### AMD Vulkan governed cohort now 11/11 comparable + claim-eligible

After the morning's promotion audit and this afternoon's cache re-run, `config/backend-workload-cohorts.json::profiles.amd_vulkan.governed` contains 11 rows, every single one `comparable=true` + `claimEligible=true`:

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (-4.33%, non-claimable per p50)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` (+11.26%)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` (+16.28%)
- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` (+48.05%)
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` (+49.90%)
- `pipeline_compile_stress` (+86.83%)
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` (+17.16%)
- `upload_write_buffer_{1kb,64kb,1mb,4mb}` (+82.57% / +91.16% / +50.74% / +93.98%)

The `governed` ⊂ `comparable` invariant (enforced by `test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles`) holds. 10 of 11 rows pass the claim gate individually; only `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 at -4.33% keeps the report-level claim status at `diagnostic`.

### Session-level AMD Vulkan program summary

From session start (2026-04-17 morning) to end:
