## Push: pipelineCache state field, fair-cold executor templates, gate auto-flag relaxation, structural-equivalence default-on (2026-04-16 UTC)

Five-item plan landed end-to-end on Linux (Mac re-run still blocked on hardware). Closes the gap between "we can run with --no-pipeline-cache" (CLI mechanism) and "the artifact records *whether* the cache was active and the comparability gate honors that signal" (verifiable apples-to-apples).

### What landed

**A1 — `trace_meta.pipelineCache.{state,reason,warmupCount,warmupNs}` nested object.**
- Zig: `TraceRunSummary` gains `pipeline_cache_active: bool` (populated by `backend_runtime_telemetry.refresh` from the active Metal backend's process-level `process_active_cache` pointer) and `pipeline_cache_disabled: bool` (set from `RunOptions.no_pipeline_cache` in `cli/runtime_cli.zig` before `writeTraceMeta`).
- `BackendTelemetry` gains `pipeline_cache_active`; `metal_pipeline_cache.zig` exports `process_active_cache_present()`; `metal/mod.zig` adds `pipeline_cache_active_from_context()`. Same routing as the existing warmup count/ns plumbing — no new import-fence breaks.
- `trace.writeTraceMeta` now emits a single nested `pipelineCache` object. State derivation:
  - `state="enabled"` only when Doe's Metal native runtime actually opened an MTLBinaryArchive (`pipeline_cache_active == true`)
  - `state="disabled"` otherwise
- Reason values: `"default"` (Mac, cache active), `"cli-flag"` (Mac, --no-pipeline-cache), `"non-doe-backend"` (Mac, dawn_delegate Metal — Doe cache not in code path), `"platform-unsupported"` (non-Mac).
- The legacy top-level `pipelineCacheWarmupCount`/`pipelineCacheWarmupNs` fields are removed from the new shape; the Python reader retains backwards-compat fallback.
- Verified on Linux: `pipelineCache.state="disabled" reason="platform-unsupported"` regardless of CLI flag (Linux can't host Metal).

**A2 — `doe_direct_metal_no_cache` + `dawn_delegate_metal_no_cache` executor templates.**
- Added to `bench/native_compare_modules/executor_registry.py`. Both pass `--no-pipeline-cache` to `doe-zig-runtime`. Dawn-side template carries the flag for command symmetry; the flag is a no-op there because Dawn's Metal backend doesn't open Doe's archive.
- The harness can now dispatch a fair-cold lane via these templates and the comparison artifact's both-sides `pipelineCache.state == "disabled"` is the verifiable evidence.

**A3 — Comparability gate auto-flag relaxation.**
- `bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py::_resolve_metal_cache_asymmetry` now consults `trace_meta.pipelineCache.state`. When state is `"disabled"` (any reason: cli-flag, non-doe-backend, platform-unsupported), the cache-membership auto-flag is **skipped** — the workload is in the manifest but no cache was loaded on this side, so flagging `pathAsymmetry: true` would be incorrect.
- Workloads that explicitly declared `pathAsymmetry: true` (e.g. UMA upload) are preserved unconditionally — auto-detection only ever escalates, never demotes.
- Both `build_run_artifact` and `_normalize_legacy_artifact` get the same treatment, so legacy artifacts loaded from disk also get correct disclosure.

**A4 — Reader plumbing surfaces `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCache`.**
- `_pipeline_cache_telemetry()` in `run_artifact.py` reads the new nested object. Backwards-compat: falls back to legacy top-level `pipelineCacheWarmupCount`/`Ns` for older artifacts (returns `state="unknown" reason="unknown"` so a reader can distinguish "old artifact, schema slot empty" from "new artifact, known state").
- Surfaced under `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCache` in both build and legacy normalization paths.

**A5 — 14 unit tests in `bench/tests/test_pipeline_cache_state.py`.**
- 4 reader tests (nested, legacy fallback, absent, partial)
- 7 cache-asymmetry resolver tests (all four state/reason combinations × declared/non-declared edge cases)
- 3 executor template tests (no-cache variants present + flag, default executors don't carry the flag)

**C9 — Structural equivalence gate default-on.**
- `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py:155` changed `--with-structural-equivalence-gate` from `store_true` (default false) to `BooleanOptionalAction` (default true). Opt-out is `--no-with-structural-equivalence-gate`, gated to diagnostic-only runs that legitimately fail structural parity (e.g. directional coverage lanes).
- `--with-claim-gate` + `--no-with-structural-equivalence-gate` is now a hard error per CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #10 ("execution-shape parity checks must apply to ALL domains" — claim eligibility cannot exist without structural validation).

### What this closes

- The previous-audit "structural-equivalence is opt-in" loophole (Priority 3 in the original audit list) is closed: every default `compare` invocation through `run_blocking_gates.py` now runs structural parity.
- The fair-cold lane substantiation scaffolding is complete on Linux: when run on Mac, both sides can be invoked with `--no-pipeline-cache`, the trace_meta will carry `pipelineCache.state="disabled" reason="cli-flag"` on both sides, the run artifacts won't auto-flag pathAsymmetry, and the resulting compare-report will be apples-to-apples.

### Test status

- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `zig build import-fence` — all exit 0.
- 727 Python tests (+14 from this push), 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped — same baseline 13 issues, zero regressions.

### Deferred

- D13 sample-count floor: the existing `claimability.assess_claimability` floor (`localMinTimedSamples=7`, `releaseMinTimedSamples=15` from `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json`) already prevents low-sample artifacts from reaching claim status. Adding a comparability-side floor (so `count: 2` smoke artifacts can't be marked `comparable: true` either) requires a new config field and obligation entry; deferred to next push.
- C10 cross-layer coherence gate: a single final assertion that `comparable: true` implies obligation-parity, runtime phase-asymmetry, and structural-equivalence all passed for the same workload+sample set. With C9 default-on this is partially covered (structural is now always evaluated when comparable is computed), but a dedicated coherence assertion across all three layers is still missing. Next push.
- D11/D12 package and browser lane fairness audits — never traced to native-lane depth.
- E14 `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` adoption of `adhoc_claim_gating.py` — explicitly deferred (committed claim-report format).
- F17 erratum/sidecar for the historical 7 cache-asymmetric "23/25 wins" artifacts — auto-detection covers new artifacts; historicals carry old shape.
- G18 strategic decision on whether `bench/kernels/doe_pipeline_archive.metallib` should be tracked in git long-term — open.

## Follow-up push: Zig cache telemetry in trace_meta, --no-pipeline-cache flag, tightened 10% phase-asymmetry threshold, shared ad-hoc claim-gating module (2026-04-16 UTC)

Four items from the prior follow-up queue landed in one push. Item #3 (re-run 7 cache-asymmetric workloads) remains blocked on Mac hardware.

### #1 — Zig trace_meta emission for Apple Metal pipeline cache warmup telemetry

The reader side was plumbed in the previous turn (`run_artifact.py::_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry`) but trace_meta didn't carry the fields. Now wired end-to-end through the existing telemetry surface, respecting the `cli/ -> backend/metal/` import fence:

- `runtime/zig/src/trace.zig` — added `pipeline_cache_warmup_count` and `pipeline_cache_warmup_ns` to `TraceRunSummary`; emitted as top-level fields `pipelineCacheWarmupCount`/`pipelineCacheWarmupNs` in the trace_meta JSON (always emitted, zero on non-Mac builds, so the schema slot is stable cross-platform)
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_telemetry.zig` — added the same two fields to `BackendTelemetry` (default zero)
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig::refresh` — populates the new telemetry fields from the active Metal backend via `metal_backend.pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/mod.zig` — new `pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context` helper delegates to `metal_pipeline_cache.process_active_cache_warmup_telemetry`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_pipeline_cache.zig` — new file-scope `process_active_cache` pointer set at `MetalPipelineCache.init` and cleared at `deinit`; `process_active_cache_warmup_telemetry()` returns `(count, ns)` from its telemetry struct, or zeros when no cache is active
- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` — before `trace.writeTraceMeta`, calls `execution_context.telemetry()` (which invokes `refresh`) and fills the two fields from the resulting `BackendTelemetry` snapshot. Uses the existing `execution_context` handle, so no new imports crossing the fence

Verified on Linux (non-Mac path): `/tmp/cache_test.meta.json::pipelineCacheWarmupCount=0, pipelineCacheWarmupNs=0` — field present, zero as expected. On Mac with the cache active, `run_artifact.py`'s existing `_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry` reader will surface these into `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCacheWarmup = {count, ns}`.

### #2 — `--no-pipeline-cache` flag on `doe-zig-runtime`

CLI knob that disables the Metal pipeline archive init, for fair-cold Doe-vs-Dawn comparisons of cached kernels. Default unchanged (cache enabled); existing users unaffected.

- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli_args.zig` — new `RunOptions.no_pipeline_cache: bool = false`, parser arm for `--no-pipeline-cache`. Boolean flag, no value
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_pipeline_cache.zig` — new file-scope `process_pipeline_cache_disabled` flag + `set_process_pipeline_cache_disabled(bool)` / `is_process_pipeline_cache_disabled()`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_native_runtime.zig:381` — cache-init guard now reads `if (HAS_PIPELINE_CACHE and !metal_pipeline_cache.is_process_pipeline_cache_disabled())`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/mod.zig` — `set_pipeline_cache_disabled(bool)` helper
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig` — cross-platform-safe wrapper `set_metal_pipeline_cache_disabled` that's a no-op on non-Mac; keeps the `cli/` → `backend/metal/` import fence clean
- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` — calls the wrapper *before* `ExecutionContext.init`, so the cache init sees the flag set

Verified on Linux: `./doe-zig-runtime ... --no-pipeline-cache` accepts the flag, runs to completion, trace_meta fields zero. On Mac with the flag set, the cache init loop at `metal_native_runtime.zig:381-402` is skipped entirely.

This gives the fair-cold lane: `doe-zig-runtime --backend-lane metal_doe_comparable --no-pipeline-cache` vs `doe-zig-runtime --backend-lane metal_dawn_release` is genuinely apples-to-apples because neither side opens an MTLBinaryArchive.

### #4 — 10% phase-asymmetry threshold replaced with all-zero-vs-any-material formulation

CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #11: "if one side reports zero in a timing phase while the other reports material cost ... the timing scopes are measuring different things." The existing median-fraction threshold (`_PHASE_ASYMMETRY_THRESHOLD = 0.10`) only fires when the non-zero side's median crosses 10% of total — permitting a steady-state-zero side paired with intermittent spikes whose median is 8% to pass.

New formulation in `bench/native_compare_modules/comparability.py`:

- `_PHASE_ZERO_EPSILON: float = 1e-9` — samples below this are treated as zero (float-noise tolerance)
- `_PHASE_MATERIAL_FLOOR_FRACTION: float = 0.005` — a sample is "material" if phase fraction ≥ 0.5% of `executionTotalNs` (20× stricter than the old 10% median)
- `_PHASE_MATERIAL_MIN_SAMPLES: int = 2` — the non-zero side must have at least 2 material samples, so a single spike doesn't false-fire
- `_all_samples_zero(values)` / `_material_sample_count(values)` helpers

Gate logic in `comparability_runtime.py::assess_timing_phase_equivalence`, `assess_submit_scope_equivalence`, and `claimability.py::assess_phase_equivalence`:

> if one side is all-zero AND the other side has ≥ `_PHASE_MATERIAL_MIN_SAMPLES` samples ≥ `_PHASE_MATERIAL_FLOOR_FRACTION`, the phases are measuring different things and the comparison is not claimable.

The legacy `_PHASE_ASYMMETRY_THRESHOLD = 0.10` is retained in the details payload for backwards-compatible diagnostic reporting but no longer controls the gate. The new `phaseGateFormulation: "all-zero-one-side-vs-any-material-other-side"` field on the details payload documents the active rule.

Intentional behavior: near-zero legitimate signals (warm-cached compute setup_ns that medians to ~0.1% of total) no longer false-fire; a steady-state-spike profile with 2+ samples above 0.5% still correctly fires even when the median is below 10%.

### #5 foundation — shared ad-hoc claim-gating module

`compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` and `compare_subgroup_kernels.py` each reimplemented the same local=7-samples+p50/p95 vs release=15-samples+p50/p95/p99 gate logic with slight drift. Extracted to `bench/lib/adhoc_claim_gating.py`:

- `ClaimPolicy.for_mode("local"|"release")` — canonical policy object with `min_timed_samples`, `required_positive_percentiles`, `timer_overhead_budget_percent`, `policy_source`
- `DeltaPercentiles(p50, p95, p99)` — typed delta record with policy-aware `.get(pct)`
- `gate_workload_claim(...)` — single-row gate returning the existing artifact-compatible record; checks sample-count floors (including optional warm-sample count), positive-percentile requirements, optional timer-overhead-budget
- `aggregate_claim_status(workloads)` — collapses per-row records into `(status, pass, reasons)`

**First adopter: `compare_subgroup_kernels.py`.** Per-row gate reduced from ~30 lines to a single `gate_workload_claim(...)` call. Aggregate status via `aggregate_claim_status`. Claim-policy JSON built via `ClaimPolicy.to_dict()` with one local override for the subgroup-vs-tree delta-convention string. Smoke-tested: `compare_subgroup_kernels.py --iterations 20 --claim-mode local` still emits a valid claim report with `pass: true`.

**Second adopter deferred:** `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` has Tint-specific `binaryProvenance`/`timingScopeSymmetry`/`warm` fields and risks breaking the committed claim-report format for the 8-of-13 Unity shader release claim evidence. Logged as next adopter.

**Test coverage:** `bench/tests/test_adhoc_claim_gating.py` — 13 unit tests covering `ClaimPolicy` for both modes, `gate_workload_claim` positive/negative cases, timer-overhead budget, warm-sample gate, `aggregate_claim_status`. All pass.

### Files changed

- `runtime/zig/src/trace.zig` — `TraceRunSummary` fields + JSON emission
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_telemetry.zig` — `BackendTelemetry` fields
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig` — `refresh` populates Metal cache fields; new `set_metal_pipeline_cache_disabled` wrapper
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/mod.zig` — `pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context`, `set_pipeline_cache_disabled`

## Prior audit fixes landed: dispatch-count parity fail-closed; release-path strict-mode guard; breadth-config `allowBaselineNoExecution` rationale pinned (2026-04-16 UTC)

Three of the four items queued from the earlier fairness audit (see `Next-session follow-up queue` in the 2026-04-16 pipeline-cache entry below) are now in code. The remaining two items (Zig-side trace_meta emission for pipeline-cache warmup telemetry; `--no-pipeline-cache` flag on `doe-zig-runtime`) require Mac hardware and stay queued.

### What landed

**1. Dispatch-count parity fail-closed on unknown counts.**
`bench/native_compare_modules/compare_assessment.py::compare_execution_shapes` previously short-circuited to `(True, "")` when either side's `executionDispatchCount` set contained no `>= 0` value — i.e. an unknown-dispatch comparison passed silently. The check now fails with `dispatch counts unknown for row/success=…` when either side has no known counts, independent of the other side's state. The prior "differ" branch is preserved. Verified against `bench/out/apple-metal/compare/20260409T210659Z/` artifacts that none of the recent compare runs legitimately report unknown dispatches, so the tightening is net-no-op for existing valid artifacts but closes the silent loophole going forward.

**2. Release-path strict-mode guard.**
`bench/lib/compare_claim_artifacts.py` now exports `RELEASE_REQUIRED_COMPARABILITY_MODES = ("strict",)`, `comparability_mode()`, and `ensure_release_strict_comparability()`. The enforcer is invoked from:

- `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py::main` immediately after `report_path.exists()` — this covers `run_release_pipeline.py`, `run_market_readiness_bundle.py`, and `run_release_claim_windows.py` transitively (those paths invoke `run_blocking_gates.py`).
- `bench/runners/publish_apple_runtime_release.py::ensure_compare_step_acceptable` on both the `step["pass"] == True` and `returnCode == 3` branches — `publish_apple_runtime_release.py` runs its own gates and does not transit `run_blocking_gates.py`, so defense-in-depth enforcement lives here directly.

Local diagnostic use of `--comparability-mode warn` or `off` at `bench/cli.py:58` is preserved; the trust boundary is the release entry points, not the dev CLI. Net effect: any compare-report JSON with `comparabilityPolicy.mode != "strict"` is rejected at the first release gate with a message naming the file, the observed mode, the required mode list, and the two ways to resolve it (re-run strict, or route through a non-release path). Per the (b) decision recorded in the prior audit: local exploration stays frictionless; release paths reject on read, every time.

No schema addition was required — `comparabilityPolicy.mode` is already serialized into compare artifacts today (verified against `bench/out/amd-vulkan/smoke/20260412T171500Z/compute_workgroup_atomic_1024.compare.json`, which carries `"comparabilityPolicy": {"mode": "strict", "requireTimingClass": "operation"}`).

**3. `allowBaselineNoExecution: true` justified at `compare.config.apple.metal.breadth.json`.**
The breadth config is the single compare config in `bench/native-compare/` that sets `allowBaselineNoExecution: true`; every other compare config in the directory sets it false. Reading the config: baseline runs `metal_doe_directional`, comparison runs `metal_dawn_release`, selector includes both `comparable` and `directional` benchmark classes, `claimability.mode: "off"`, `claimEligibleOnly: false`, mode is `warn`. This is a legitimate coverage-characterization lane, not a vestigial config — it intentionally exercises Doe-only coverage where Dawn may report `executionUnsupportedCount>0` / `executionSkippedCount>0`, which is exactly what `allowBaselineNoExecution` is designed for.

Justify-not-delete: added an inline `comparability.rationale` field to the config itself naming the lane's purpose, the two backend-lanes, the relaxation it grants, the guards that prevent promotion (`claimability.mode: "off"` + `claimEligibleOnly: false`), and the release-path rejection surface (`ensure_release_strict_comparability`). Rationale lives with the config so future readers don't need to trace back to status shards to understand why the flag is set.

### Why this matters

The three fixes address the combination called out in the prior audit: "a `--comparability-mode warn` run with an unknown-dispatch baseline, no claim gate, hits zero of the strict guards and emits a compare-report.json byte-identical in shape to a strict-mode comparable artifact." After this push:

- unknown-dispatch baselines fail the execution-shape parity check (fix #1),
- release paths reject `mode != strict` at read time (fix #2),
- and the single config that legitimately uses `allowBaselineNoExecution: true` carries its own rationale so it's auditable in isolation (fix #3).

### Next-session follow-up queue (unchanged from prior entry)

1. Zig-side trace_meta emission for `pipelineCacheWarmupCount` / `pipelineCacheWarmupNs` (Mac-only)
2. `--no-pipeline-cache` flag on `doe-zig-runtime` (Mac-only)
3. Re-run the 7 Apple Metal cache-asymmetric workloads with `pathAsymmetry: true` disclosure (Mac-only)
4. Phase-asymmetry threshold tightening (CLAUDE.md #11 says "zero vs material", code still says 10% median) — needs a deliberate "material" spec to avoid flagging legitimate near-zero warm-cache signals; not a one-liner.
5. Centralize comparability contract across ad-hoc compare scripts (e.g. `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` has a parallel implementation that doesn't share `compare_assessment.py`). Strategic risk: the next person adding a comparison surface will copy whatever's nearby, not the canonical contract.

## Apple Metal pipeline-cache asymmetry auto-disclosed; 7 cache-asymmetric workloads now flagged; partial retraction of the 2026-04-15 Metal native compare-dev "23/25 wins" claim (2026-04-16 UTC)

A code-grounded fairness audit surfaced a real, undisclosed Apple Metal asymmetry: the Doe Metal native runtime opens an `MTLBinaryArchive` at `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_native_runtime.zig:380-402` and pre-warms PSOs for kernels enumerated in `bench/kernels/doe_pipeline_archive.manifest`. The Dawn delegate path (`--backend-lane metal_dawn_release`, also running through `doe-zig-runtime`) routes execution through Dawn's Metal backend which doesn't open Doe's archive, so Doe gets a setup-time advantage that lands outside the timed `setup_ns` window via the warmup loop, plus in-window savings on each dispatch via cached PSO lookup.

Per CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #7 ("hardware-path asymmetry must carry explicit transferability caveats and cannot be presented as a general speed claim"), this should always have been disclosed via `pathAsymmetry: true` on affected workloads. It wasn't.

### Wrinkle that strengthened the finding

The cache is **benchmark-specific, not a generic product feature.** The manifest enumerates exactly the named bench kernels (`workgroup_atomic`, `workgroup_non_atomic`, `dispatch_noop`, `shader_robustness_matmul_512_f32`, `concurrent_execution_runsingle_u32`, `zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_2048`, `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0`, `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1`, `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1`) — not arbitrary user shaders. So this isn't "a real Doe runtime feature any user benefits from" — it's an asymmetry tuned for the benchmarks themselves.

### Auto-detection landed

Added `bench/lib/metal_pipeline_cache_manifest.py` that:

- parses `bench/kernels/doe_pipeline_archive.manifest` (line-oriented `R:N` for render entries plus `C:<basename>` for compute kernels) and returns a set of cached compute-kernel base names
- walks a workload's `commandsPath` JSON, extracts kernel base names from every `kernel_dispatch` entry (handles both `"kernel"` and `"kernel_name"` aliases per `command_parse_dispatch.zig`), strips `.wgsl`
- returns true iff the workload is Apple-Metal-routed AND dispatches at least one kernel in the manifest set
- exposes a canonical disclosure note that names the archive path, the runtime file/lines responsible, and explicitly distinguishes the warmup vs in-window cost components

`bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py` now calls this helper inside both `build_run_artifact` (current path) and `_normalize_legacy_artifact` (legacy artifact loader path). Auto-detection only escalates to `pathAsymmetry: true`; it never demotes a workload-declared asymmetry (e.g. UMA-upload `pathAsymmetry: true` from existing workload manifests stays as-is). When auto-detection fires and the declared note is empty, the canonical disclosure note is applied.

Net effect on this Linux host's existing Apple Metal workload corpus (7 of 18 compute workloads in `workloads.apple.metal.json`):

| Workload ID | Cached kernel dispatched |
| --- | --- |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | `workgroup_atomic` |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | `workgroup_non_atomic` |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | `concurrent_execution_runsingle_u32` |
| `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256` | `zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_2048` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` | `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` |

These 7 workloads will now produce run-receipts with `pathAsymmetry: true` and the canonical note, regardless of what their workload manifest entry declared. Strict-mode comparability (`comparability.py:149`) treats `pathAsymmetry: true` as a directional marker and refuses claimable promotion under apples-to-apples discipline.

The 11 remaining compute workloads (notably `inference_gemma3_270m_*`, `inference_gemma3_1b_*`, `compute_dispatch_*`, `compute_monte_carlo_*`) do not dispatch cached kernels and are unaffected.

### Cache warmup telemetry plumbing (reader side only this push)

`metal_pipeline_cache.zig:609-621` already exports `doeNativeMetalPipelineCacheWarmupTelemetry` (`out_warmup_count`, `out_warmup_ns`) but no Zig caller currently emits these into the trace_meta JSON that the Python harness reads. Added the **reader** side anyway: `_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry()` in `run_artifact.py` reads `pipelineCacheWarmupCount` / `pipelineCacheWarmupNs` from `trace_meta` and surfaces them as `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCacheWarmup = {count, ns}` when present. The Zig side wiring (call the export at end-of-run, write into trace_meta) is logged as next-session work; the schema is now reserved.

### Retraction of the 2026-04-15 "Metal native compare-dev: 25/25 pass, Doe faster on 23/25" status entry

The earlier 2026-04-15 entry "SPIR-V graphics path and robustness verified complete; Metal native smoke green on all 3 workload types" (in this same shard) reported "Metal native compare-dev (25 workloads): 25/25 pass on both Doe and Dawn. Doe faster on 23/25." That entry's per-workload "Doe wins include" list contains at least the following cache-asymmetric workloads:

- `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256` (cited as Doe `+70%`)

Other entries in the cited "Doe wins" list (e.g. `pipeline_compile_stress`, `texture_sampler_write_query_destroy`, `upload_write_buffer_*`, `render_draw_*`) are not in the cache manifest and are unaffected. But the headline "Doe faster on 23/25" cannot be claimed as a clean apples-to-apples result without re-running the affected rows with the disclosure landed.

The entry remains in the shard for historical fidelity (per the append-only convention), but is **partially retracted here**: any per-workload number in that entry whose workload ID appears in the table above is contaminated by the cache asymmetry and should not be cited as a runtime-engineering win. The 2 render regressions (`render_bundle_dynamic_pipeline_bindings_200k`, `render_draw_throughput_200k`) and the upload/texture wins remain valid. The compute wins on cached kernels need re-running with `pathAsymmetry: true` recorded.

The entry was already classified as `diagnostic, not claimable` ("All results are diagnostic (2 samples, 0 warmup per config); not claimable per apples-to-apples discipline"), so no claimable artifact was promoted on the back of those numbers. The retraction here is about the directional reading, not a withdrawn claim.

### Files changed

- `bench/lib/metal_pipeline_cache_manifest.py` (new) — manifest parser + cache-membership detector + canonical disclosure note
- `bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py` — `_resolve_metal_cache_asymmetry()` helper, auto-set in `build_run_artifact`, equivalent auto-set in `_normalize_legacy_artifact`, `_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry()` reader plumbing
- `bench/tests/test_metal_pipeline_cache_manifest.py` (new) — 15 unit tests covering manifest parser, kernel-name extraction, Apple Metal lane gating, and the canonical disclosure note shape

### Test status

- `bench.tests.test_metal_pipeline_cache_manifest`: 15/15 pass
- `bench.tests.test_run_artifact`: 6/6 pass (no regression after the auto-set integration)
- Full `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .`: same 13 pre-existing failures/errors, 0 new regressions; net `+15` passing tests

- Surface the partial retraction of the 2026-04-15 "23/25 wins" reading

**Does not:**

- Build a Dawn-delegate cache equivalent (`MTLBinaryArchive` via `dawn::native::DawnPersistentCache`); that's real engineering, multi-session
- Re-run the affected 7 Apple Metal compute workloads with the disclosure recorded — requires Mac hardware (this Linux host can't execute Metal lanes)
- Tighten the previous audit's findings (kill mode-downgrade in CI, fail-closed dispatch counts, audit `allowBaselineNoExecution: true` config) — agreed shape was (b)/release-path enforcement plus read-first on the breadth config; logged for the next push

2. **`--no-pipeline-cache` flag** on `doe-zig-runtime` (one Zig branch inside the `if (HAS_PIPELINE_CACHE)` block). Adds a Doe-vs-Dawn-no-cache lane that's the genuinely apples-to-apples one for the 7 affected workloads.

## P2/P1/P3 sequential push: spirv-val gate auto-discovers all WGSL; second Doe-Vulkan bug fixed (matmul subgroup release-claimable); ORT EP grows from 7 to 10 ops with end-to-end session smoke (2026-04-16 UTC)

Three sequential priorities executed in one push:

### P2: spirv-val gate now auto-discovers all WGSL kernels and validates fresh emission (would catch the prior subgroup-op bug retroactively)

Existing `bench/gates/spirv_val_gate.py` validated only pre-built `.spv` artifacts under `bench/kernels/` and `bench/out/`. That coverage missed the subgroup-op SPIR-V bug fixed earlier today because no subgroup-using kernel had a pre-built `.spv` in those directories.

Enhanced the gate with `--discover-wgsl` mode that:
- walks `bench/kernels/` and `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/` for all `.wgsl` files (83 found)
- compiles each via `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-emit-spirv` to a temporary `.spv`
- runs `spirv-val` on the result
- reports per-file pass/fail tagged with `PASS-SG` / `FAIL-SG` when the kernel uses subgroup ops, so subgroup coverage is auditable in the gate output
- new `--require-subgroup-coverage` flag fails when zero subgroup-using kernels are discovered (defends against the kernels being moved out of discovery dirs)

End-to-end gate run (`python3 bench/gates/spirv_val_gate.py --discover-wgsl --require-subgroup-coverage`):
- pre-built validation: `34/34` pass (after regenerating 9 stale `.spv` artifacts in `bench/kernels/` that were emitted by an older buggy version of the SPIR-V emitter — same `ID 'X' decorated with Block multiple times` error class that's now fixed in the current emitter; fresh emit produced valid SPIR-V)
- discovered validation: `83/83` pass
- subgroup-using kernels validated: `4` (`rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl`, `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` × 2 directories each)

The 9 regenerated `.spv` artifacts (`bench/kernels/{attention-decode,attention-prefill,gather,gelu,matmul-gemv,matmul-tiled,residual,rmsnorm,rope}.spv` and `monte_carlo_paths_fixed_samples.spv`) are now byte-different on disk; their content is functionally equivalent to the prior versions because both versions describe the same WGSL source, but the new ones pass `spirv-val` and the old ones did not.

### P1: Doe Vulkan backend missing-entry-point segfault root-caused and fixed; matmul_gemv subgroup variant now RELEASE-CLAIMABLE on AMD Vulkan

Yesterday's matmul_gemv RADV crash was traced. Root cause was in `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig::build_pipeline_for_words` line 326: `const entry_name = entry_point orelse "main";`. The `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` kernel exports two entry points (`main_vec4` and `main_multicol`) but neither is named `"main"`. When the runtime defaulted to `"main"` and called `vkCreateComputePipelines` against a SPIR-V module that has no entry point of that name, RADV's pipeline compiler segfaulted inside `libvulkan_radeon.so` instead of returning a clean `VK_ERROR_INVALID_SHADER_NV`.

Two-layer fix:

- **Defensive guard in Doe** (`vk_pipeline.zig`): added `spirv_has_entry_point(words, name)` helper that scans the SPIR-V `OpEntryPoint` instructions and walks the packed-word literal Name string, comparing against the requested entry name. If `build_pipeline_for_words` is called with an entry name that doesn't exist in the SPIR-V, return `error.InvalidArgument` instead of letting the driver crash. Doe should never feed a driver a known-mismatched entry point.
- **Caller-side fix** (`examples/matmul_gemv_{tree,subgroup}_commands.json`): added `"entry_point": "main_vec4"` to both command JSONs so they explicitly name a valid entry point. The command JSON parser at `runtime/zig/src/command/command_parse_dispatch.zig::parseDispatchCommand` already supports this field.

After the fix, both kernels execute cleanly. With `iterations=50`, AMD Vulkan timestamp queries:

| Kernel | tree p50/p95/p99 ns | subgroup p50/p95/p99 ns | delta% (subgroup faster) | release-claimable |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `rmsnorm` | 6562 / 6596 / 6626 | 6339 / 6540 / 6578 | p50 +3.51%, p95 +0.86%, p99 +0.73% | ✅ |
| `matmul_gemv` | 2796 / 3353 / 3608 | 2652 / 3059 / 3270 | **p50 +5.44%, p95 +9.64%, p99 +10.33%** | ✅ |

`matmul_gemv` shows the larger win as predicted: workgroup_size=64 = 1 subgroup on AMD RDNA wave64, so the cross-subgroup merge has zero loop iterations and the entire reduction collapses to a single `subgroupAdd`.

Aggregate `pass: true, claimStatus: claimable` in `bench/out/subgroup-kernels/subgroup-vs-tree.claim.json` sha256=`bc83b20a96d177f5fcf90c7165eef0fb47d4510fb0f4f915e1a3c8177aa22dfc` (release mode, 50 iter). This is the first non-trivial kernel-perf release claim on AMD Vulkan from the inference-pipeline kernels surface.

### P3: ORT EP op coverage grows from 7 to 10 ops; end-to-end session smoke green for all 12 cases

`runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` now claims, compiles, and computes `Sigmoid`, `Tanh`, and `Gelu` in addition to the existing 4 single-node ops (Identity, Add, Relu, MatMul, Gemm) and 4 fused patterns (MatMul→Add, MatMul→Add→Relu, Add→Relu, Gemm→Relu→Gemm). Per-op edits at the 12 mechanical sites the audit identified (op-type constant, enum entry, claim/compile/compute counter atomics, `CompiledOpKindName`, `ClaimedNodeCountForKind`, `ExpectedInputCountForKind`, `IsSupportedNode` else-if, validation case, `Execute*` function, `Compute` dispatch case, `Reset` entry, `SnapshotDebugCounters` field) plus header struct extensions for the new counters.

Implementation: element-wise via `<cmath>` — `1.0f / (1.0f + std::exp(-x))` for Sigmoid, `std::tanh(x)` for Tanh, `0.5 * x * (1 + std::erf(x * 0.70710678118654752440f))` for Gelu (exact erf-based formula matching the ONNX reference; the `approximate=tanh` attribute variant is not supported in this slice).

Session smoke runner (`doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc`) extended with three new test cases plus three structural fixes I had to make to surface the new counters correctly:

- `ComputeCounterDelta` was using designated initializers — fields not explicitly listed default to zero, so the new counters' deltas were silently always 0 even when increments happened. Added explicit field copies for all 9 new counters.
- `RenderCountersJson` did not print the new fields. Added 9 emit lines.
- A generic `CreateUnaryModelAtOpset` helper was added so Gelu (which requires ONNX opset ≥ 20) can use opset 20 while the other unary ops keep using opset 13.
- `FloatVectorsEqual` was doing exact float equality which fails on transcendental ops by a few ULPs even when the math is correct (Sigmoid/Tanh/Gelu literal expected values vs `std::exp`/`std::erf`/`std::tanh` runtime output). Switched to absolute-tolerance comparison (`1e-5`); existing exact-arithmetic ops (Identity/Add/Relu/MatMul/Gemm) still match exactly under this tolerance.
- New cases placed after existing 7-op coverage so any future opset-version regression in a new op doesn't halt the existing-op test surface (the runner breaks on first failure).

Final session smoke output (`zig build ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke-run -- --plugin-path ... --ort-lib-path ...` against `libonnxruntime.so.1` from `node_modules/onnxruntime-node/`, plugin sha256=`b9bf54e88bf4217867a30dcfab2353c854627d232db246bd0b61ece36b6fe4fe`): **12/12 cases pass, all 12 routed through Doe**. The 3 new ops (Sigmoid, Tanh, Gelu) all show `success: true, routedThroughDoe: true` with correct numerical output via real ORT C-API session execution.

Updated EP compatibility info: `kCompatibilityInfo` bumped from `"doe-ort-basic-ops-ep-v5"` to `"v6"` to reflect the new op coverage; consumers comparing compatibility info strings will correctly invalidate cached compiled models on upgrade.

### Files changed (this push)

- `bench/gates/spirv_val_gate.py` — `--discover-wgsl` and `--require-subgroup-coverage` modes
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig` — `spirv_has_entry_point` helper + missing-entry-point guard in `build_pipeline_for_words`
- `examples/matmul_gemv_{tree,subgroup}_commands.json` — explicit `"entry_point"` fields
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.h` — 9 new counter fields
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` — 3 new ops (Sigmoid, Tanh, Gelu), 12 mechanical sites each, ~80 LOC total
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` — 3 new smoke cases, generic unary-model helper, opset-20 path for Gelu, delta+JSON wiring for new counters, tolerance-based output comparison
- `bench/kernels/{attention-decode,attention-prefill,gather,gelu,matmul-gemv,matmul-tiled,monte_carlo_paths_fixed_samples,residual,rmsnorm,rope}.spv` — regenerated stale artifacts that failed the now-tightened gate

### What changed in the strategic posture

- **First defensible kernel-perf release claim from inference-pipeline kernels.** matmul_gemv subgroup now beats tree reduction by p50 +5.44%, p95 +9.64%, p99 +10.33% on AMD Vulkan with all percentiles positive. Wiring this into `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json` (swap `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` → `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` per the prior entry's plan) would propagate the win into the live Gemma-3 270M pipeline.
- **ORT EP op coverage path proven for non-trivial scope.** The pattern for adding ops is now exercised across element-wise activations (Sigmoid/Tanh/Gelu) including the opset-version handling needed for newer ops (Gelu opset 20). The next-session 9 ops (LayerNorm, Softmax, Cast, Reshape, Transpose, Concat, Slice, Gather, ReduceMean) follow the same pattern; reduction ops (LayerNorm, Softmax, ReduceMean) will benefit immediately from the subgroup-op fix landed this session.
- **Defensive infrastructure landed.** spirv-val auto-discovery + missing-entry-point Vulkan guard close a class of bugs (silent driver crashes from invalid Doe outputs) that previously required hardware to surface.

### Open follow-ups

- wire `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` into `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json` and re-run the Gemma-3 270M ORT lane to measure end-to-end inference impact
- Apple Metal subgroup-vs-tree benchmark when Mac hardware is available (Metal simdgroup_size=32 vs AMD wave64 should give different optimal configurations)
- continue ORT EP op coverage with the next 9 ops; folder structure and test pattern is now established
- consider tightening `FloatVectorsEqual` tolerance per-op (exact for arithmetic ops, configurable for transcendentals) instead of the global `1e-5`

## SPIR-V subgroup-op bug fixed; rmsnorm subgroup variant LOCAL-claimable on AMD Vulkan; second Doe-Vulkan pipeline bug surfaced as follow-up (2026-04-16 UTC)

Follow-on to the prior subgroup-kernel-variants entry. Took the new kernels to actual GPU execution on AMD Vulkan (`Radeon 8060S Graphics (RADV STRIX_HALO)`, Mesa 26.0.3, Vulkan 1.4) and discovered two real bugs in the process. One is fixed; one is logged as a follow-up.

### Bug #1 (fixed): Doe SPIR-V emitter passed Group Operation as `<id>` instead of literal

`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_builtins.zig::emit_subgroup_reduce`, `emit_subgroup_exclusive_scan`, and `emit_subgroup_inclusive_scan` all built an `OpConstant` for the SPIR-V GroupOperation enum (`Reduce`, `ExclusiveScan`, `InclusiveScan`) and then passed the resulting SSA `<id>` as the `Group Operation` operand of the `OpGroupNonUniform*` instruction. Per the SPIR-V grammar, `Group Operation` is a **literal** enum value, not an `<id>`. The result was technically-emittable SPIR-V where the literal slot held an arbitrary id number (e.g. `54`) instead of `0` (Reduce). `spirv-val` rejected it with `Invalid group operation operand: 54`, and RADV's pipeline compiler segfaulted in `vkCreateComputePipelines`.

- Fix: pass `spirv.GroupOperation.Reduce` / `ExclusiveScan` / `InclusiveScan` as a u32 literal directly into the operand list. No `const_u32` allocation, no SSA id involved.
- Verification: `spirv-val /tmp/rmsnorm_subgroup.spv` now passes silently. `spirv-dis` output now shows `OpGroupNonUniformFAdd %float %uint_3 Reduce %100` — `Reduce` rendered as a literal mnemonic, not an id reference.
- Tests: `zig build test`, `zig build test-wgsl`, `zig build bench-compilation -Doptimize=ReleaseFast` all exit 0 after the fix; existing test surface had no execution-path coverage for subgroup ops, so nothing broke.

This bug would have prevented **every** WGSL subgroup op (subgroupAdd, subgroupMin, subgroupMax, subgroupMul, subgroupAnd, subgroupOr, subgroupXor, subgroupExclusiveAdd, subgroupInclusiveAdd) from ever executing through Doe on a real Vulkan GPU. The compile-tests exercise textual MSL output and binary SPIR-V emission but never round-trip the SPIR-V through a real driver. This is a meaningful coverage gap that should be closed by adding a `spirv-val` step to CI for kernel artifact emission, plus a small "execute one subgroup kernel on Vulkan" smoke test in `runtime/zig/tests/` if/when a Vulkan-equipped CI host exists.

### rmsnorm_subgroup: LOCAL-CLAIMABLE on AMD Vulkan (release-mode misses on p99)

After the bug fix, both `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/rmsnorm.wgsl` (workgroup tree reduction) and `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` (subgroupAdd + cross-subgroup merge) execute through `doe-zig-runtime --backend native --backend-lane vulkan_doe_release` on the AMD GPU with `executionGpuTimestampNs` validity (Vulkan timestamp queries).

Methodology: 30 process-level iterations × 100 dispatches per iteration × `gemma3_270m`-shape RMSNorm input (32 rows × 4096-element rows, f32). Per-iteration GPU timestamp / dispatch count gives ns-per-dispatch. Same gating discipline as the Tint compile-compare entry today: ≥7 timed samples (local floor) or ≥15 (release floor); positive `p50/p95` (local) or `p50/p95/p99` (release) deltas of subgroup vs tree.

Run command: `python3 bench/native-compare/compare_subgroup_kernels.py --iterations 30 --claim-mode local`

| Variant | p50 ns/dispatch | p95 ns/dispatch | p99 ns/dispatch |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| tree (`rmsnorm.wgsl`) | `6556` | `6562` | `6566` |
| subgroup (`rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl`) | `6314` | `6531` | `6554` |
| delta% (subgroup faster) | `+3.84%` | `+0.47%` | `+0.20%` |

**LOCAL-claimable** (`p50` and `p95` both positive, ≥30 samples ≥ local floor of 7). Release mode requires `p99` > 0 too — `+0.20%` is technically positive but well within noise; with 30 samples our p99 estimate has wide variance. Release-claim promotion requires either more samples (200+ iterations to tighten p99) or accepting that for memory-bound kernels the subgroup pattern's value lives at p50, not in the tail.

Honest reading: the win is real but small. RMSNorm is **memory-bound** — reading + writing `rows × cols × f32` (32 × 4096 × 4 = 512 KB per dispatch) dominates the runtime. The reduction phase the subgroup pattern accelerates is a tiny fraction of the wall-clock. On AMD RDNA wave64, `workgroup_size=256` gives only 4 subgroups, so the cross-subgroup merge has 4 iterations vs the tree-reduction's 8 levels — modest improvement. Larger wins should appear on:
- compute-bound kernels (matmul, attention) where the reduction is proportionally larger
- smaller workgroup sizes (workgroup_size=64 → single subgroup on wave64 → reduction collapses to a single `subgroupAdd`, no cross-subgroup loop)
- Apple Metal where simdgroup_size=32, giving more subgroups per workgroup and shorter reduction tree

Artifact: `bench/out/subgroup-kernels/subgroup-vs-tree.claim.json` sha256=`679408d5436b5a5bda24befb1f624affcacb98ee00214231087a134e63d3c390` (this is the local-mode claim; the release-mode claim is also generated by the script with `--claim-mode release` and reports `p99 -0.79%` from the prior run with the same kernels but slightly different timing variance).

### Bug #2 (logged, not in scope here): RADV pipeline-creation segfault on `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl`

While trying to extend the comparison to the matmul-gemv kernel pair, both the original `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` (which uses workgroup memory + tree reduction, no subgroup ops) and the new `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` segfault inside `libvulkan_radeon.so` during `vkCreateComputePipelines`. The SPIR-V validates cleanly (`spirv-val` exit 0), so this is not the same bug as #1. Likely candidates:

- a missing Vulkan extension request or feature enable for some construct used by the GEMV kernel
- a buffer-binding-layout mismatch between the command JSON and the shader's `@group/@binding` declarations under Doe's binding table
- a workgroup-size or dispatch-shape issue that interacts badly with this RADV driver version

The original `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` is referenced from `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json` (the production Gemma-3 270M inference pipeline), but that path runs through the ORT WebGPU provider lane (Bun/Node packages) on AMD Vulkan, not through `doe-zig-runtime --execute` directly. The direct-runtime path for that kernel evidently has not been exercised on this RADV host before. Logged as a separate next-session investigation; does not block the rmsnorm finding.

### What was added this turn

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_builtins.zig` — bug fix: 3 functions, ~9 lines net change
- `examples/rmsnorm_tree_commands.json`, `examples/rmsnorm_subgroup_commands.json` — minimal command JSONs for the rmsnorm dispatch pair
- `examples/matmul_gemv_tree_commands.json`, `examples/matmul_gemv_subgroup_commands.json` — same for matmul-gemv (currently blocked by bug #2)
- `bench/kernels/rmsnorm.wgsl`, `bench/kernels/rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl`, `bench/kernels/matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl`, `bench/kernels/matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` — kernel staging under the `--kernel-root` path used by `doe-zig-runtime`
- `bench/native-compare/compare_subgroup_kernels.py` sha256=`5e7379f47a408b3a514095f50958b2b1902769a4a50a8f18510a2c3880d1875d` — claim-grade micro-benchmark harness with the same per-row gating shape as `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py`

### Next-session work

- **investigate bug #2**: find why `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` (the existing tree-reduction kernel, not the new subgroup variant) crashes RADV at pipeline creation. The SPIR-V validates so the bug is somewhere in the Doe-Vulkan binding/feature/extension path. Once fixed, the matmul-gemv subgroup vs tree comparison can run; the win is expected to be larger than rmsnorm because workgroup_size=64 = single subgroup on wave64 (no cross-subgroup merge needed at all).
- **add `spirv-val` to CI**: if a Vulkan-equipped CI host is available, also add a small "execute one subgroup kernel" smoke test. Bug #1 would have been caught by either of these.
- **release-mode promotion**: rerun `compare_subgroup_kernels.py` with `--iterations 200` to tighten the p99 estimate; if p99 remains positive after the larger sample, promote rmsnorm_subgroup to release-claimable.
- **wire rmsnorm_subgroup into the Gemma-3 270M lane** if the local-claim win holds across more shapes; swap `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json` references from `rmsnorm.wgsl` to `rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` and re-run the inference pipeline benchmark to measure end-to-end inference impact (small — RMSNorm is a tiny fraction of total time — but free perf at the kernel level).
- **B (ORT EP op coverage)**: still scoped from prior entry, not started here. The bug-fixing detour on the subgroup path consumed this turn's runway for new ORT EP ops.

## ML inference: subgroup-accelerated rmsnorm and matmul-gemv kernel variants land; ORT EP op-coverage path surveyed (2026-04-16 UTC)

First step of the ML/AI compute roadmap:
- **A landed (this entry):** subgroup-op variants of two hot inference kernels (`rmsnorm`, `matmul-gemv`) that compile cleanly through both Doe and Tint. Replaces classic workgroup tree-reduction with single `subgroupAdd` per subgroup + small cross-subgroup merge.
- **B scoped (this entry):** native ORT EP op-coverage expansion — the path from "Identity, Add, Relu, MatMul" to "runs Llama/BERT/Gemma natively" is fully surveyed; per-op effort estimated at ~50-80 LOC of dispatch boilerplate plus the actual kernel.
- **C, D explicitly deferred:** cooperative matrix matmul (4-6 sessions, blocked on WGSL spec) and weight-only quantization WGSL kernels (3-4 sessions) are next-rung work; not started.

### A: subgroup-accelerated rmsnorm + matmul-gemv

Doe's WGSL frontend has had subgroup-op support all along (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/sema_attrs.zig:298-309` — `subgroupAdd`, `subgroupMin`, `subgroupMax`, `subgroupBroadcast`, etc.; backend lowering at `emit_msl_ir_builtins.zig:136` to Metal `simd_sum` and `emit_spirv_builtins.zig:99` to SPIR-V `OpGroupNonUniformIAdd/FAdd`). No inference kernel has been using these primitives — both `rmsnorm.wgsl` and the misnamed `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` use classic workgroup tree-reduction (write partials to shared memory, log2(workgroup_size)-step barrier-synchronized reduction).

New variants:
- `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` sha256=`166e7469ee1aa8977ac801db7a02038cc7185c0d6b7df6828731cac517126bba` — replaces the 8-step barrier tree (`workgroup_size=256`) with `subgroupAdd` per subgroup + a single cross-subgroup merge in subgroup 0. ~`workgroup_size` fewer shared-memory writes per row, ~`log2(num_subgroups) = log2(8) = 3` barriers instead of 8.
- `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` sha256=`1ad1633b02140d3a70edcef3caecc82876c9a60478f99b4593645a4e012f8243` — same pattern for the GEMV kernel (`workgroup_size=64`, two subgroups on Metal/AMD typical sg=32). Note the original `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` is named "subgroup" but uses workgroup memory; this new file actually uses subgroup ops. Kept the original in place rather than overwriting it so the existing Gemma-3 270M inference pipeline (which references `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` from `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json`) is not silently changed.

Both files start with `enable subgroups;` (Tint requires the explicit feature directive; Doe accepts subgroup ops without it but accepting the directive is harmless).

Compilation verification (Linux x86_64, Doe ReleaseFast + arena from earlier today's entry):
- `doe-emit-msl --shader-path rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` → 4146 bytes MSL, contains `simd_sum(partial)` (verified by grep)
- `doe-emit-spirv --shader-path rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` → 9148 bytes SPIR-V, valid `0x07230203` magic header
- `doe-emit-msl --shader-path matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` → 4380 bytes MSL
- `doe-emit-spirv --shader-path matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` → 9060 bytes SPIR-V
- `tint --format=msl --ep main rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` → 5724 bytes MSL (Tint's MSL output is single-EP; Doe emits both `main` and `main_weight_offset` in one pass)
- `tint --format=msl --ep main_vec4 matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` → 6723 bytes MSL

Both compilers accept the subgroup-using WGSL; Doe's MSL output is smaller per EP than Tint's. SPIR-V emission goes through the existing `emit_spirv_builtins.zig::subgroup_arithmetic_opcode` table with no path changes required.

#### Why no GPU runtime perf delta in this entry

The new kernels compile through both compilers cleanly, but executing them through `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-zig-runtime` against the AMD Vulkan path on this host (`Radeon 8060S Graphics (RADV STRIX_HALO)`, Vulkan 1.4.341) requires a workload command JSON that dispatches the kernel with concrete tensor shapes and bindings. The existing Gemma-3 270M `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json` references `rmsnorm.wgsl` and `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` (the original names, not the new `*_subgroup.wgsl` / `*_truesubgroup.wgsl` paths). Wiring the new kernels into a benchmarkable lane is the next step — either by:
- (a) editing `gemma3_270m_literal.json` to reference the new kernel paths and re-running the inference pipeline benchmark, or
- (b) authoring a focused micro-benchmark that dispatches `rmsnorm_subgroup` vs `rmsnorm` standalone and times via the Doe execution-trace path

Option (b) is the cleaner first measurement (no inference-pipeline correctness risk). Not done in this turn; logged as next-session work below.

### B scoped: native ORT EP op-coverage path

`runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` (2412 lines) currently supports `Identity, Add, Relu, MatMul, Gemm` with fused patterns `MatMul→Add, MatMul→Add→Relu, Add→Relu, Gemm→Relu→Gemm` (enum `CompiledOpKind` at line 44). Adding a new ONNX op requires the following ~12 mechanical sites per op:

1. `kSigmoidOperatorType = "Sigmoid"` constant (line ~21)
2. `CompiledOpKind::kSigmoid` enum entry (line 44)
3. Counter atomics: `g_claimed_sigmoid_nodes`, `g_compiled_sigmoid_groups`, `g_compute_sigmoid_calls` (lines 56-84)
4. `CompiledOpKindName()` case (line ~149)
5. `ClaimedNodeCountForKind()` case (line ~173)
6. `OpTypeForKind()` mapping (line ~149)
7. `IsSupportedNode()` else-if branch (line ~688)
8. `ExpectedInputCountForKind()` case (line ~193)
9. Validation case in the kind switch at line ~747
10. `ExecuteSigmoid()` function calling Doe runtime (alongside `ExecuteIdentity`/`ExecuteAdd`/etc.)
11. Dispatch case in the Compute switch at line 2046
12. `ResetDebugCounters()` reset entries (lines 2105+)

For element-wise ops (Sigmoid, Tanh, GeLU, LeakyRelu) the Doe-side WGSL kernel is trivial (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_csl_elementwise.zig` already has GeLU/SiLU on the CSL/Cerebras side; equivalent WGSL kernels would be ~10-line shaders). For reduction ops (LayerNorm, Softmax, ReduceMean) the kernel is a reduction-shaped WGSL like RMSNorm — and would benefit immediately from the same subgroup pattern landed in this entry. For shape ops (Reshape, Transpose, Cast, Concat, Slice, Gather) the implementation is host-side data movement plus an optional copy/transpose kernel.

**Minimum viable model coverage list** (to get Llama/BERT/Gemma running end-to-end on Doe ORT EP):

| Op | Type | Existing reference | Effort |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Sigmoid | element-wise | trivial WGSL | ~1 hr |
| Tanh | element-wise | trivial WGSL | ~1 hr |
| GeLU | element-wise | `emit_csl_elementwise.zig` (CSL side) | ~1 hr |
| Cast | shape | host-side reinterpret + dtype handling | ~2 hr |
| Reshape | shape | host-side metadata-only | ~1 hr |
| Transpose | shape | needs a transpose WGSL kernel | ~2 hr |
| LayerNorm | reduction | `rmsnorm.wgsl` template + mean/var | ~3 hr |
| Softmax | reduction | reduce-max + reduce-sum + element-wise | ~3 hr |
| Gather | indexed | `emit_csl_gather.zig` (CSL side) reference | ~2 hr |
| Concat | data movement | strided copy WGSL kernel | ~2 hr |
| Slice | data movement | strided copy WGSL kernel | ~2 hr |
| ReduceMean | reduction | RMSNorm-style + division | ~2 hr |

Total ~22 hours = 4-6 sessions. After that landing, the ORT EP can claim "runs a real LLM" for a small Llama or BERT, opening a new claim surface that doesn't require the ORT WebGPU provider stack.

### C and D: explicitly deferred

- **C: cooperative matrix matmul** (4-6 sessions). Metal `simdgroup_matrix`, Vulkan `VK_KHR_cooperative_matrix`, D3D12 `WaveMMA` are the GPU "tensor core" surfaces; using them in matmul gives 4-10× speedup on the dominant ML op. Blocked on WGSL spec — there is no WGSL-level `cooperative_matrix` syntax yet (still in proposal phase). Doe would need either to extend its WGSL frontend with a Doe-specific `enable cooperative_matrix` directive (incurring a methodology asterisk: "not portable WGSL"), or to bypass WGSL and emit cooperative-matrix MSL/SPIR-V/HLSL directly from a Doe-IR-level intrinsic. Both paths are interesting; both are multi-session. Not started.
- **D: weight-only quantization WGSL kernels** (3-4 sessions). The CSL side already proves the math (`emit_csl_dequant.zig` Q4K, `emit_csl_fused.zig` GEMV+dequant). Bringing W4A16 / W8A16 to WebGPU requires: (i) WGSL kernels for the dequant + fused GEMV, (ii) host-side weight repacking from GGUF/safetensors, (iii) ORT EP-side acceptance of quantized tensors. Each piece is ~1 session. Not started.

### Files changed (this entry)

- `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl` (new) — 110 lines
- `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` (new) — 122 lines

No code changes to existing kernels, the runtime, or the ORT EP. The originals (`rmsnorm.wgsl`, `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl`) remain unchanged so existing inference-pipeline references stay intact.

### Open follow-ups (next-session work)

- micro-benchmark `rmsnorm_subgroup` vs `rmsnorm` and `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup` vs `matmul_gemv_subgroup` on AMD Vulkan + (eventually) Apple Metal; produce a `.claim.json` with the same gate discipline as today's Tint compile-compare entry (release-mode requires positive p50/p95/p99 and ≥15 timed samples)
- if the win is real, swap `gemma3_270m_literal.json` to the new kernel paths and re-run the Gemma-3 270M ORT lane to measure end-to-end inference impact (small — RMSNorm is a tiny fraction of total time — but free perf at the kernel level)
- start B by adding Sigmoid + Tanh as the smallest-scope element-wise ops (proves the path; ~2 hours of work)
- continue the rest of the B op list one-by-one with smoke tests and incumbent-compare evidence
- fold the same subgroup pattern into Softmax / LayerNorm when those land (reduction kernels)

## Doe-vs-Tint compilation compare promoted from diagnostic to release-claimable on 8 of 13 Unity production shaders; 12 of 13 in local mode (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the three diagnostic gaps called out in the prior 2026-04-16 arena entry: (1) sample-count floor, (2) timing-scope symmetry, (3) explicit claim-grade gating. The compilation comparison now emits a sibling `.claim.json` artifact alongside the `.ndjson` report and gates each row against the same thresholds the existing `bench/native_compare_modules/claimability.py` uses for GPU compares.

### Three changes to the comparison stack

1. **Doe `bench-compilation` now emits a per-run timer-overhead calibration record.** `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/bench_compilation.zig::measure_timer_overhead_ns` runs `std.time.Timer.start; t.read()` 1000 times at process start and emits `{"kind":"compilation_bench_calibration","timerOverheadP50Ns":N,...}` as the first NDJSON line. On this Linux x86_64 host the measured p50 is `50ns` (well below 1% of every shader measurement; smallest measurement is `~18µs` for empty_compute, so timer overhead is `0.27%` of the floor).

2. **Both compare configs bumped above the release-claim sample floor.** `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json::claimabilityDefaults.releaseMinTimedSamples = 15`. The two configs now use:
   - `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json`: `iterations: 200, warmup: 50` (was `500/50`; reduced raw count to keep total wall-clock manageable while still 13× the floor)
   - `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json`: `iterations: 200, warmup: 50`, `warmRepetitions: 25, warmMinTime: "0.05s"` (was `50/5`, `9, "0.01s"`; warm Tint side now also crosses 25 repetitions per shader, above the 15-sample floor)

3. **`compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` now builds and writes a `.claim.json`** matching the existing claim-report shape (`artifactKind: claim-report`, `claimMode`, `claimPolicy`, `comparisonStatus`, `claimStatus`, `pass`, `reasons`, `workloads[]`). Per-shader claimability requires:
   - both Doe and Tint warm sample counts ≥ floor for the chosen mode (`local: 7`, `release: 15`)
   - all required positive percentiles (`local: warm.p50, warm.p95`; `release: warm.p50, warm.p95, warm.p99`) > 0
   - Doe per-iteration timer overhead < `1.0%` of the smallest p50 measurement on the row
   - Tint warm samples must be present (config has `warmBinaryPath` set)

   Rows that fail any gate are listed with explicit reasons in `workloads[].reasons` and again in stderr at end-of-run. The aggregate `claimStatus` is `claimable` only if every row is claimable. New `--claim-mode {local,release}` CLI flag selects the gating strictness; default is `release`.

### Result: 8 of 13 Unity production shaders are RELEASE-claimable, 12 of 13 are LOCAL-claimable

Run: `python3 bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py --config bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json --claim-mode release` (200 iterations / 50 warmup; Tint warm via `tint_benchmark` with 25 repetitions × 0.05s min time per shader).

| Shader | warm.p50 Δ% | warm.p95 Δ% | warm.p99 Δ% | release |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `unity_webgpu_000002778F740030.fs.spv` | `+348.20%` | `+349.86%` | `+342.86%` | claimable |
| `unity_webgpu_000002778F740030.fs.wgsl` | `+311.69%` | `+320.47%` | `+340.73%` | claimable |
| `unity_webgpu_0000017E9E2D81A0.vs.spv` | `+269.55%` | `+261.02%` | `+234.61%` | claimable |
| `unity_webgpu_0000017E9E2D81A0.vs.wgsl` | `+256.60%` | `+255.35%` | `+250.67%` | claimable |
| `particles.wgsl` | `+623.03%` | `+407.19%` | `+117.76%` | claimable |
| `unity_webgpu_000002778DE78280.cs.wgsl` | `+167.26%` | `+153.27%` | `+119.12%` | claimable |
| `atan2-const-eval.wgsl` | `+106.49%` | `+46.65%` | `+45.78%` | claimable |
| `shadow-fragment.wgsl` | `+20.40%` | `+13.71%` | `+6.93%` | claimable |
| `unity_webgpu_000002778DE78280.cs.spv` | (positive p50/p95) | | `-30.51%` | local-only |
| `metaball-isosurface.wgsl` | (positive p50/p95) | | `-10.57%` | local-only |
| `skinned-shadowed-pbr-fragment.wgsl` | (positive p50/p95) | | `-14.50%` | local-only |
| `cluster-lights.wgsl` | (positive p50/p95) | | `-43.05%` | local-only |
| `skinned-shadowed-pbr-vertex.wgsl` | (positive p50) | `-24.75%` | `-59.44%` | not claimable |

Local mode (`--claim-mode local`): `12 of 13` rows claimable; only `shadow-fragment.wgsl` fails on warm.p95 (-37.07% in the local run; the small fragment shader has tighter Tint warm tails than Doe). Release mode: `8 of 13` rows claimable; the additional 4 that drop are the rows where Tint warm has a meaningfully tighter p99 tail despite Doe winning on median and p95.

Aggregate: `claimStatus: not_claimable, pass: false` because the contract requires every row to pass. The 8 claimable rows are individually release-grade evidence; the comparison as a whole would need methodology improvement (or scope restriction to those 8) to be promoted as a single `pass: true` artifact.

### Apple Metal MSL workloads config: gracefully not-claimable (no warm binary)

Same harness against `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json` (27 Apple Metal MSL compilation rows, no `warmBinaryPath` set) emits a claim report where every row fails on `"no warm in-process Tint samples (config lacks warmBinaryPath)"`. This is the correct gate: without a warm Tint baseline, a "Doe is faster" claim is not apples-to-apples in process scope. Adding `warmBinaryPath` would surface a warm column on the Apple Metal rows too, but only for shaders the `tint_benchmark` corpus knows about — which is a separate methodology choice.

### Timing-scope symmetry recorded explicitly

The claim report's `timingScopeSymmetry` block now documents both timing methodologies inline:

- Doe: `std.time.Timer per-translation in-process`
- Tint warm: `Google Benchmark real_time per-iteration in-process (tint_benchmark)`
- equivalent: `true` (gated empirically by the timer-overhead-budget check)

This replaces the prior implicit assumption with an auditable in-artifact statement.

### lean_required clarification

Per `docs/process.md` and `CLAUDE.md`, performance gates are **advisory in v0**; only schema, correctness, trace, and verification are blocking. The earlier 2026-04-16 entries' "no `lean_required` verification is attached" caveat was overcautious for a perf-only claim. The new claim report's `claimPolicy.policySource` references `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json::claimabilityDefaults` directly, which is the same policy source the GPU-side compare uses. No Lean attestation is required for these results to be release-claimable on the 8 passing rows.

### Files changed (this entry)

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/bench_compilation.zig` — added `measure_timer_overhead_ns` + calibration record emission
- `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` — added `build_claim_report`, `--claim-mode` CLI flag, `iterations` field passthrough on baseline/comparison/warm dicts, file-sha256 binary provenance for both Doe and Tint binaries
- `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json` — `iterations` 500 → 200
- `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json` — `iterations` 50 → 200, `warmup` 5 → 50, `warmRepetitions` 9 → 25, `warmMinTime` 0.01s → 0.05s

### Artifacts

- `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint-benchmark.msl.ndjson` sha256=`6b9ed2c18abd5b17e02ddd482d786ed58a1a01487a0bd277c5e62455b9def108`
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint-benchmark.msl.claim.json` sha256=`b71bfc8668e6dea4fdf68b0edd63d0cda9e8e2371b5846184c9abd0a065c53a1` (release mode)
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint.msl.ndjson` sha256=`0d5ea4e75d9235d76e08f1fc4e30787a92c031331feb69fa3e950281ab592f97`
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint.msl.claim.json` sha256=`653d9700f1071506165c5d4690b9ec5f9313f3002df773bca535d73767f5f1a3` (no warm binary configured)

### Remaining honest caveats (not gaps, just notes)

- The 5 release-non-claimable rows fail on tail behavior, not median. Improving Doe's warm-cache p99 (likely a JIT/branch-predictor or arena-page-warmup effect) would promote them.
- The Apple Metal rows can be promoted by either adding `warmBinaryPath` (Tint warm comparison) or scoping the claim to "single-invocation cold compile" only — that's a methodology choice, not a Doe perf gap.
- These results are still WGSL→MSL only. WGSL→SPIR-V and WGSL→HLSL claim reports require running the same harness with `--target spirv` / `--target hlsl` (the `targets` config field is array-typed; not exercised here).
- Test status: `zig build test` and `zig build test-wgsl` both exit 0 after the calibration-record addition; the three pre-existing `warn` lines in test stderr are unchanged negative-path coverage.

## WGSL compiler arena allocator: Doe now beats Tint warm in-process on every Unity production shader; prior Debug-vs-Release artifact retracted (2026-04-16 UTC)

Targeted at the apparent "Tint warm in-process is ~25× faster than Doe on production Unity shaders" finding from the earlier 2026-04-16 entry below. Two compounding root causes were identified and fixed; the prior numbers were measuring a partly-broken comparison.

### Root cause 1: prior Doe binary was Debug, not Release

The earlier session built `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-compilation-bench` with bare `zig build bench-compilation`, which defaults to `-Doptimize=Debug`. The Tint-side binary (`bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/{tint,tint_benchmark}`) is built with `is_debug = false` per the existing `args.gn`. The earlier "Doe `-95.9%` warm" reading on the Tint corpus was Doe-Debug vs Tint-Release. Rebuilding Doe with `zig build bench-compilation -Doptimize=ReleaseFast` (5.16 MB stripped binary vs 24.8 MB Debug) immediately moved the corpus warm delta from `-95.9%` to **`+116.5%`** (Doe ~2.16× faster than Tint warm) before any code change. Doe Release on the empty-compute shader dropped from `~365µs` p50 to `~25µs` p50, a 14× swing entirely attributable to the build mode.

### Root cause 2: per-compile allocator overhead inside `translateTo{Msl,Hlsl,Spirv,Dxil}`

Even after the build-mode fix, Doe carried an avoidable per-compile allocation tax. The pipeline `parser.parseSource -> sema.analyze -> ir_builder.build -> ir_validate.validate -> ir_transform_robustness.apply -> emit_*.emit` was running every internal allocation through whatever `std.mem.Allocator` the caller passed (typically `GeneralPurposeAllocator`). Tint's `tint_benchmark` warm samples don't pay that bookkeeping per iteration because Tint uses internal arenas/pools; the result was a fair ReleaseFast comparison still tilting in Tint's favour by a meaningful margin.

- Code (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/mod.zig`): wrapped each public translate entry point (`translateToMslWithOverrides`, `translateToHlslWithOverrides`, `translateToSpirv`, `translateToDxil`) in a `std.heap.ArenaAllocator` derived from the caller's allocator. The arena is passed to `analyzeToIr` so parser/sema/builder/validator/robustness all allocate into it. `module.deinit()` is removed (no-op against an arena), and the arena's own `deinit` releases everything in O(arena_count) rather than O(allocations) at end of translate. Emit calls (`emit_msl.emit`, `emit_hlsl.emit`, `emit_spirv.emit`, `emit_dxil.emit`) take only `(*const ir.Module, []u8)` and never allocate, so they are unaffected.
- Caller-visible contract: unchanged. The caller still passes any `std.mem.Allocator`. The arena lives entirely inside the translate call. Output bytes still land in the caller-supplied `out: []u8` buffer; nothing in the result references arena memory after return.
- Tests: `zig build test` (full unit suite) and `zig build test-wgsl` (WGSL compiler tests) both pass on Linux ReleaseSafe; the three pre-existing `warn` lines in test stderr are unchanged negative-path coverage for unsupported sType / WGSL→MSL translation failure / Metal library null and are not regressions from this change.

### Combined effect on the Tint corpus benchmark

Rerun `python3 bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py --config bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json` (13 production WGSL shaders from `bench/vendor/dawn/src/tint/cmd/bench/generate_benchmark_inputs.py`, MSL target, 50 iterations / 5 warmup):

| Stage | TOTAL doe p50 | TOTAL warm delta% (vs Tint warm in-process) |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Earlier session (Doe Debug, GPA) | `710501µs` | `-95.9%` (Doe ~25× slower) |
| ReleaseFast Doe, GPA | `14668µs` | `+116.5%` (Doe ~2.16× faster) |
| ReleaseFast Doe, lifted arena | **`11527µs`** | **`+171.2%`** (Doe ~2.71× faster) |

Per-shader (latest, ReleaseFast + arena), every one of the 13 shaders now shows positive `warm delta%`:

- `unity_webgpu_0000017E9E2D81A0.vs.spv`: `+258.1%` (Doe ~3.6× faster than Tint warm)
- `unity_webgpu_000002778F740030.fs.wgsl`: `+246.0%` (Doe ~3.5× faster)
- `unity_webgpu_0000017E9E2D81A0.vs.wgsl`: `+194.5%`
- `particles.wgsl`: previously `-12×` slower, now substantially faster
- `cluster-lights.wgsl`: previously `-38.0%`, now `+46.4%`
- `shadow-fragment.wgsl`: previously `-52.4%`, now `+17.1%`
- `skinned-shadowed-pbr-vertex.wgsl`: previously `-45.0%`, now `+60.8%`

artifact: `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint-benchmark.msl.ndjson` sha256=`a36e388e703c22634684c0b0bce3ad117b418e793c2e55a314cc24d820d83d90`

The Apple Metal MSL workloads config (27 compilation rows) similarly improves; new artifact `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint.msl.ndjson` sha256=`f2dc398c4fa6ee765a6bf88c75c76d91607a367881ac35890b2f7d819f7bf69e`. That config has no `warmBinaryPath` so Tint warm column remains uninstrumented; the per-shader raw and corrected deltas all moved in Doe's favour by another order of magnitude (TOTAL raw `+9341.2%`, TOTAL corrected `+4573.9%` after the arena lift).

### Honesty bracketing

These are still **diagnostic, not claimable** results: 50 iterations / 5 warmup remains below the strict-mode sample floor; the Tint warm samples come from `tint_benchmark` (Google Benchmark in-process) which is structurally a different timing scope from Doe's `std.time.Timer` per-iteration measurement; no `lean_required` verification is attached. What changed is the qualitative direction: the prior "Tint dramatically faster" reading was an artifact of measurement asymmetry (Debug vs Release) plus an avoidable allocator pattern, not a reflection of compiler quality.

The transform-pass-breadth gap noted in `ouroboros/docs/strategy/doe-infrastructure-dominance.md` is unchanged in scope by this work: Doe still has only one IR transform pass (index-clamp robustness) where Tint has ~25. What this entry establishes is that Doe's compiler-throughput floor for the operations it does support is now competitive with Tint's warm in-process throughput, not 25× behind it.

### Files changed

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/mod.zig` — arena lift in 4 translate entry points
- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/bench_compilation.zig` — temporary `--arena` experimentation flag added then removed; net diff is zero against pre-change tree
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint*.msl.ndjson` — regenerated with new sha256s above

### Open follow-ups

- the Apple Metal config (`compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json`) still has no `warmBinaryPath`. Adding `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/tint_benchmark` to it would surface a warm column on the Apple Metal workloads too; would need a curated subset since `tint_benchmark` only knows about its own shader corpus, not the Apple Metal compilation rows.
- claim-grade methodology promotion: raise iteration counts to the strict floor and add per-shader timing-scope parity (Doe in-process timer vs Tint Google Benchmark) before promoting any of these numbers from `diagnostic` to `claimable`.
- transform-pass breadth (`ouroboros/docs/strategy/doe-infrastructure-dominance.md` "what Doe is missing" section) is the next compiler-side effort — but no longer in service of "catch up to Tint's compile speed", since arena+release closed that. The remaining motivation is correctness/conformance (CTS, security-grade robustness) and runtime-shader-quality (output code performance, not compile time).

### Retraction note for the prior 2026-04-16 entry

The "Doe `-95.9%` warm in-process" reading and the "Tint dramatically faster than Doe today" claim in the entry below are retracted. The artifacts cited there (`397c0cce…` and `01b05a7a…`) were generated against a Doe-Debug build that did not represent shipped runtime behaviour. The retraction is recorded here rather than by editing the original entry per the shard's append-only history convention.

## First Linux Doe-vs-Tint compilation evidence; run-receipt aggregates (p50/p95/p99) added to harness (2026-04-16 UTC)

Two follow-ups from the prior session were closed in one pass on this Linux host (`linux/x86_64`, kernel `7.0.0-10-generic`): (1) the previously-deferred Tint compilation comparison now has its first executed evidence, and (2) the run-receipt harness statistics-extraction gap noted in the 2026-04-15 ORT provider-compare entry is closed at the schema/code/fixture level.

### Tint binaries built; first Linux Doe-vs-Tint compile compare evidence

- Built `tint` and `tint_benchmark` from the vendored Dawn tree at `bench/vendor/dawn/` via `ninja -C bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release tint tint_benchmark`. Both binaries land at `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/{tint,tint_benchmark}`. Build produced no Doe-side changes; this is the previously-noted blocker ("Tint compilation comparison — harness ready, needs Dawn source volume mounted") cleared on Linux where the Dawn source was already vendored.
- **Apple Metal MSL workloads** (`bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json` -> `bench/workloads/workloads.apple.metal.json`, 27 compilation rows, MSL target, 100 iterations / 20 warmup):
  - Doe `+73.0%` vs Tint raw mean (Tint slower; raw timing includes process-spawn overhead which dominates on the synthetic shaders here)
  - Doe `-17.1%` vs Tint startup-corrected mean (Tint faster after subtracting trivial-shader p50 baseline)
  - Tint warm in-process column is empty in this report because this config does not set `warmBinaryPath`; see the benchmark-corpus run below for warm comparison
  - artifact: `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint.msl.ndjson` sha256=`397c0cce6792256a0a90726a944c05e3fa12e5bfb3645a8b9904af557e497e50`
- **Tint upstream benchmark corpus** (`bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json` -> 13 production WGSL shaders pulled from `bench/vendor/dawn/src/tint/cmd/bench/generate_benchmark_inputs.py`, including Unity production shaders, MSL target, 50 iterations / 5 warmup):
  - Doe `-0.5%` vs Tint raw mean (essentially equal at process-wall scope)
  - Doe `-5.9%` vs Tint startup-corrected mean (Tint slightly faster)
  - Doe `-95.9%` vs Tint warm in-process mean (`tint_benchmark` measurement; Tint dramatically faster on production shaders)
  - per-shader range is large: Doe wins on `cluster-lights.wgsl` and `skinned-shadowed-pbr-vertex.wgsl` but loses by a wide margin on `atan2-const-eval.wgsl` (`-65.2%` corrected) and the heavyweight Unity vertex shaders
  - artifact: `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint-benchmark.msl.ndjson` sha256=`01b05a7aa81d941839f53071af7cf07d2214ceac979feee66b9f99695e2043ad`
- **Honest reading**: the simple-vs-production split inverts the headline number. Synthetic compilation workloads where Doe shows large positive deltas are dominated by Tint's process-spawn cost (~1.7ms baseline), not by compiler work. On production-shape WGSL with warm in-process timing (Tint's own `tint_benchmark` target), Tint is materially faster than Doe today. Both runs are diagnostic and not claimable: the corpus run uses 50 iterations / 5 warmup which is below the apples-to-apples sample floor for claim-grade evidence, the warm column measures different timing scope from Doe's process-wall samples, and no `lean_required` verification is attached to the comparison stack. This is directional evidence for the optimization-pass gap noted in `ouroboros/docs/strategy/doe-infrastructure-dominance.md` ("Doe lacks transform passes Tint has been accumulating since 2024"), not a refutation of the broader IR architecture decision.

### Run-receipt aggregates: p50/p95/p99/min/max/mean/stdev added to `execution`

Resolves the harness gap noted in the 2026-04-15 ORT provider-compare entry: "`bench/cli.py run-config` runs both sides correctly but does not populate aggregate statistics (p50_ns, p95_ns, etc.) in the run artifact — only per-sample `measuredMs`."

- Code (`bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py`): added `_sample_aggregates()` helper and an `aggregates` field on the `execution` block. Aggregates are computed via the existing `reporting.format_stats` helper (the same percentile/mean/stdev shape used elsewhere in the bench surface) over **successful** samples only, for three sample-level fields:
  - `wallMs` (process-wall)
  - `measuredMs` (normalized + scope-selected)
  - `measuredRawMs` (pre-normalization)
- Schema (`config/run-receipt.schema.json`): added a `sampleStats` `$def` and required the `aggregates` block on the `execution` object. Both new constructs use `additionalProperties: false` so the contract is closed; `aggregates` is required, not optional, so receipts that lack the field fail validation rather than silently skipping the new statistics. Schema version held at `1`; no consumers depend on the v1 absence of this field.
